[2025-12-17T06:20:26Z] Ryan Colaço: Just my opinion... Maybe most others see this differently..and not meant at all negatively... Just thought I'd express a wish I felt, and leave it to your and majority opinion to accept/reject. ↵ But I do find the UPSC/Indian style of questions (the concept of GK and general awareness) not quite fun. ↵ When I was in school, a lot of quizzes used to be this way... And, although I did okay on those, I never felt the _thrill or love_ I associate with quizzing today. ↵ The first time I saw a quiz with well-crafted questions... ↵  The high I felt when the answer was revealed ( and the fact that, whether I got it right or wrong, didn't even matter) blew my mind. What was strange was that it was usually the same 'lurn'... Just the effort put in framing the question and how it forces you to think laterally, to use the _exact same_ knowledge, was 🤌.... ↵ I've been hooked since then. ↵ Finding KV and his work reconnected me to that (and a lot of other people who felt the same thrill) again... ↵ So, I love that the discourse and questions here align with that + keeps feeding that habit. Even the "guess the Bizzaro/movie" etc. forces you to do the same kind of lateral thinking (where you feel that the answer could have been guessed, if you only thought it through a bit more or on a different track). ↵ So, my suggestion: would love to lurn the things in these questions... But would you be okay with kinda testing the same concept, but framed in a bit of a second-order, treasure-hunt way? ‎<This message was edited>

[2025-12-18T18:31:53Z] Ryan Colaço: Yup yup! ↵ Bat and seabird guano is incredibly rich in nitrogen, phosphate, and potassium, which are key for fertilizers. In the 19th century, European and American agriculture was expanding rapidly, and Guano was basically the “super fertilizer” of the era—it could massively increase crop yields. ↵ It was also used for gunpowder production (the nitrate content made it militarily useful). ↵ Some guano-rich islands made companies and investors fortunes. A single guano shipment could fetch high prices in Europe or the U.S. ↵ THis act essentially allowed U.S. citizens to: ↵ -Claim uninhabited islands with guano deposits anywhere in the world. ↵ -Gain exclusive rights to mine guano on those islands. ↵ -The U.S. government could intervene militarily to protect such claims.
